After the Min and Hakka Merchants Refused to Load the Taishun Ship, China Merchants Bureau Declared a Price Reduction to Attract Customers; Freight Rates Reduced by 25% from Today; Sanbei and Other Companies Expressed Dissatisfaction

The New Sound Society reported that since the China Merchants Bureau's ships sailing on the Shanghai-Fujian line were refused loading by the Fujian merchants, the business volume decreased with each departure. Yesterday, a declaration was specially issued, detailing the process and implementing a 25% reduction in freight rates, which caused dissatisfaction among Sanbei, Chang'an, Yihua, and other companies. The details are recorded as follows:

Price Reduction to Attract Customers

The China Merchants Bureau issued a public declaration soliciting Fujian goods yesterday, saying, "It is found that in the past, due to various reasons, the treatment of various merchant guilds in the transportation of Fujian goods by our Bureau's ships may have been uneven. Now that our Bureau has been changed to a state-owned enterprise, we should pay more attention to the maintenance of domestic shipping and the convenience of cargo and passengers. The treatment of various merchant guilds when reporting the loading of goods should also be the same. In the future, all legitimate merchants who come to the Bureau to report the loading of Fujian goods will be sincerely welcomed. Furthermore, our Bureau's ships started sailing to Fujian the earliest. Now, in order to expand business, we should strengthen ties with various merchant guilds and work together for progress. From now on, all freight rates between Fujian and Shanghai will be reduced by 25% on the gross amount on a trial basis to attract more customers. Our Bureau's Taishun ship has been sailing on the Shanghai-Fujian route for a long time. Its speed and load capacity are all suitable. It is hoped that various merchant guilds and firms will report and load Fujian goods on our Bureau's ships at any time. Not only will our Bureau's business gradually develop, but the prosperity of the Fujian market may also benefit slightly. This is hereby declared, and it is hoped that it will be appreciated."

Dissatisfaction Among Competitors

The ships of various shipping companies operating between Shanghai and Fuzhou include the China Merchants Bureau's Taishun ship, the Sanbei Company's Wanxiang ship, the Yihua Company's Jiesheng ship, the Chang'an Company's Hua'an ship, and the NingShao Company's Yongxing ship, totaling five ships from five companies. Now, the NingShao Company's Yongxing ship has run aground and sunk in the Zhejiang waters. After the China Merchants Bureau's Taishun ship was refused loading by the Fujian merchants, the Shanghai Shipping Association took on the role of mediation and tried to dredge the situation. It was originally scheduled to hold another meeting yesterday to continue the dredging. Now, after the China Merchants Bureau specially declared a 25% reduction in freight rates, various companies such as Sanbei are deeply dissatisfied and may be affected by the China Merchants Bureau's price reduction and follow suit with price reductions.

The Municipal Government Sets Up Seven Offices for Poor People to Borrow Capital

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and the War Zone Rehabilitation Committee organized the "Poor People Borrow Capital" program to help poor people and regulate finance so that the social economy can circulate. The Central News Agency reporter specifically asked the person in charge of the Social Affairs Bureau who manages the "Poor People Borrow Capital" program about this matter yesterday. The conversation is as follows:

The Circumstances

Before January 28th, the city's "Poor People Borrow Capital" program was all organized by the Social Affairs Bureau, divided into two capital borrowing offices in Nanshi and Zhabei. The Social Affairs Bureau had original funds of about 40,000 yuan, which has increased to 45,000 yuan over the years due to interest profits. However, in the Zhabei area, it has been difficult to recover capital after the war. Poor people in Jiangbei have either fled or died, making it difficult to trace, so the loss is estimated to be more than 3,000 yuan. Currently, in the Zhabei area, there is already a "Poor People Borrow Capital" office organized by the War Zone Rehabilitation Committee, which is larger in scale and entrusted to the Social Affairs Bureau for management, so the Bureau has stopped the old "Poor People Borrow Capital" office in Zhabei and only manages one office in Nanshi.

Current Situation

The War Zone Rehabilitation Committee's "Borrow Capital" office is funded by 250,000 yuan from the Ministry of Finance and another 170,000 yuan from previous horse racing charity tickets, totaling 420,000 yuan. However, the Social Affairs Bureau's agency has received an actual amount of 360,000 yuan. The rest has not been fully received because it is not urgently needed. Among this amount, 200,000 yuan was taken by the Education Bureau and allocated for war zone school relief. As for the "Borrow Capital" offices, there are seven in total: (1) Zhabei District, (2) Jiangwan District, (3) Yinhang District, (4) Yinxiang District, (5) Zhenru District, (6) Wusong District, (7) Pengpu District.

Types of Loans

There are four types of loans available at the "Borrow Capital" office: the first type is "Poor People Borrow Capital", the second type is "Agricultural Borrow Capital", the third type is "House Building Borrow Capital", and the fourth type is "Small Industry Borrow Capital". "Agricultural Borrow Capital" uses the farmer's land deeds as collateral. "House Building Borrow Capital" is one of the disaster area restoration plans, so that disaster victims can restore their old businesses in the Zhabei area. "Small Industry Borrow Capital" is available for small businesses such as sock factories and small businesses dealing with cotton, wool, copper, iron, and glass utensils. Loans can be borrowed from the office without interest, ranging from 50 yuan to 500 yuan, and are repaid in four years. As for "House Building Borrow Capital", the Jiangwan District has taken the most, totaling 100,000 yuan.

Repayment Method

The nature of the Social Affairs Bureau's "Borrow Capital" office and the War Zone Rehabilitation Committee's "Borrow Capital" office are slightly different. The "Borrow Capital" office organized by the Committee is purely charitable, while the Social Affairs Bureau's office is to regulate the social economy and is not entirely a charitable undertaking, so a small amount of interest must be charged. For example, if a small business vendor borrows 20 yuan, they are ordered to repay 1 yuan per day until it is paid off, with an interest of 23 cents. However, in order to prevent them from escaping and evading debt, their residence must be clear, and they must be ordered to ask a shop as a guarantor. If necessary, the Public Security Bureau will still jointly manage the matter with the Bureau.

Haichang Company's Haishun Ship Shelters from Wind in Huidao Island; People and Ships are Safe and Sound; Should be Able to Return to Shanghai Within a Few Days

The Haichang Shipping Company at 79 Gongguan Road in this port has two ships, Haiping and Haishun, sailing to Dalian, Yingkou, and other places in northern China. The Haiping ship is being repaired in Dalian. The Haishun ship, due to sluggish business in northern China recently, loaded a large batch of flour and grain in Shanghai on the 16th of this month and set off for Xiamen to unload. On the 23rd, after unloading passengers and cargo in Xiamen, it went to Keelung to add coal and came to Shanghai. The company planned that the ship would load flour and set off for Yingkou immediately after returning to Shanghai. It was calculated that the ship would only take three days to travel from Xiamen via Keelung to Shanghai. According to the usual practice, it should have arrived in Shanghai on the morning of the 25th or 26th, but it had not arrived in Shanghai by the 27th. There have been strong winds in the South China Sea recently, and the company was very anxious, so it sent a radio inquiry. The radio station was unable to respond, and the company was even more worried. So, yesterday morning, it sent people to inquire about the news everywhere and urgently telegraphed the agency in Xiamen to inquire. It received a reply at 1 pm, which said, "(Original telegram) Sheltering from the wind at anchor in Huidao Island." The company was relieved after receiving this telegram. It is said that Huidao Island is outside Xinghua in Fujian. Currently, the ship is still there and has not yet weighed anchor. It should be able to return to Shanghai in the next two or three days. Once it arrives in Shanghai, it is said that it will still sail to Niuzhuang according to the scheduled sailing schedule.

Winning of Zero-Value Construction Lottery Tickets is Not Affected in Any Way

Since the Aviation Highway Construction Lottery Office announced that if the first prize is won in the returned ticket numbers of the second phase lottery, the government will donate the 500,000 yuan prize money that the first prize itself should have received to the ticket buyers as a special prize, and re-draw until it is won in the sold tickets, most ticket buyers have been concerned about the second phase lottery, which is issued in strips. If the number of the first prize is drawn, only one or two strips or three or four strips are sold, and the remaining strips of the same number have been returned and accepted by the government, then how will it be handled? According to the person in charge of the office, although the second phase lottery is issued in strips, it has been agreed with the general managers of the sales agents in various provinces that if a lottery number (i.e., one ticket) has been sold according to the strips, regardless of whether nine strips or only one strip has been sold, all remaining unsold strips, from one strip to nine strips, cannot be returned and will be counted as sold. Therefore, there is no problem at all, and ticket buyers can rest assured.

Woman Shen Yuqin Sues Her Brother for Division of Property; Reconciliation Deadline Set

Shen Yizhen, residing at No. 279 Yulin Lane, Shanhai Pass Road, works as a builder. After the death of his father, Shen Muying, he seized all of the over 300,000 (currency unspecified) in inheritance, treating it as his own, disposing of and mortgaging it at will. He completely disregarded his two sisters who had the right to inherit the property, prompting his sister Shen Yuqin to hire lawyers Zhan Jifeng and Zhan Yigang to file a lawsuit for division of property in the First Special District District Court. She requested a judgment ordering the defendant to hand over all movable and immovable property for division into three shares. Shen Muying and his wife had one son and two daughters. The son is Yizhen. Besides Yuqin, another daughter is married with the surname Huang. Although Yuqin is of considerable age, she remains unmarried and currently resides at No. 22 Datong Lane, Baker Road. Muying was a carpenter by trade, and came to Shanghai in his thirties to make a living. Initially quite poor, he established himself through diligence and thrift over twenty years. He died of illness this June. His son, Yizhen, harbored ulterior motives and did not include the names of his two sisters in the obituary. Subsequently, he gradually sold or mortgaged the property. After discovering this, Yuqin felt that her father's bones were not yet cold, yet her brother was acting this way. If she remained silent, her inheritance rights would inevitably be completely infringed upon. She then requested the court to allow the division of her father's property equally among the three siblings. The initial trial resulted in a ruling that the plaintiff, the defendant, and their married sister all had equal inheritance rights, and the request to divide the inheritance into one-third shares was deemed appropriate, and the court ruled in favor of the plaintiff. Unexpectedly, Shen Yizhen was unconvinced and again hired lawyers Zhang Shizhao and Peng Yuanxun, who defended him in the initial trial, to file an appeal with the Second Branch of the High Court, claiming that the property was not inherited from his father but was acquired by him personally. He requested the original judgment be overturned, but also secretly asked people to mediate a reconciliation with Shen Yuqin to avoid legal sanctions. Until yesterday afternoon, when the Second Branch of the High Court convened a hearing, lawyer Peng still appeared in court, stating that the appellant and the appellee were siblings and were currently in mediation, requesting an adjournment, etc. Lawyer Zhan Jifeng also appeared in court on behalf of Shen Yuqin, stating that since the appellant had requested an adjournment for reconciliation, she would not object. Presiding Judge Han Zuzhi, in order to expedite the case to avoid backlog, ordered that the hearing begin on one hand, and reconciliation efforts continue on the other. Lawyer Peng first presented the appellant's reasons for the appeal, and lawyer Zhan then refuted them point by point. Judge Han then announced a deadline for the appellant to reach a reconciliation within three days. If no agreement was reached by then, the verdict would be announced on the afternoon of November 1st.

Anti-Japanese Comrade's Downfall: Liang Tongfang Pulls a Rickshaw, Returning Home from the Military with Unfulfilled Aspirations, Grieving as He Gazes North at Yan and Yun

After the September 18th Incident, many patriotic youths in the country joined the military, traveling thousands of miles to the Northeast to aid the national crisis. However, the national situation is like a game of chess, unpredictable. After the signing of the North China Ceasefire Agreement, those who had gone to the Northeast with aspirations could not fulfill their wishes and returned south in disappointment. A reporter from the Fuxing Society met yesterday with Liang Tongfang, a former member of the 19th Route Army Student Corps and the 3rd Brigade of the Shanghai Civilian Volunteer Army. He returned from the Northeast and has fallen to the point of pulling a rickshaw in Shanghai to make a living. The details are recorded below:

Liang's Background

Liang is 24 years old, from Shangyu, Zhejiang. He studied in his hometown as a child, but was unable to continue his studies due to poverty. In his youth, he was introduced by a relative to work at Jinhe Qianzhuang on Fuzhou Road in this city. He continued to study at night school, and was therefore highly valued by the manager of the Qianzhuang. After the January 28th Incident, Liang joined the Civilian Volunteer Army, and later entered the 19th Route Army as a student in the accompanying corps, under the command of Brigade Commander Weng Zhaoyuan.

Going North to Participate in the War

After Liang completed his training under General Weng Zhaoyuan, he joined the Shanghai Student Army Northeast Volunteer Group. He departed from Wuxi and went north to Beiping, residing in the first dormitory of Feng Yong University inside Xizhimen. On January 5th of this year, he departed for Yuguan and was stationed in Haiyang Town. He was then reorganized into the 8th Independent Brigade. One month later, he set off for Jiumenkou, reaching the first line of defense and engaging in anti-Japanese warfare.

River Changes and Reorganization

Later, Tang Yulin, Chairman of Rehe Province, retreated without a fight, and there was no defensible terrain in front. Liang and his comrades retreated from Jiumenkou to Beiping, and were reorganized into the Liaojihei People's Army Support Association Engineering Training Team, stationed at Wanshoushan in Xiyuan for training. Before long, the Tanggu Truce was signed. Feng Yuxiang suddenly rose up in Chahar to resist the Japanese, and the Engineering Training Team also went to Chahar from Beiping to participate. Liang went along, which was his second anti-Japanese campaign.

Coming to Shanghai for Negotiations

Subsequently, due to the central government's specific plans for resisting Japan, Feng voluntarily withdrew from Dolun. Liang was ordered to go south to Shanghai to negotiate with various parties. Before leaving, Yao Zirang's niece, Yao Ruifang, specifically introduced her brother, lawyer Yao Zhaoli, and personally wrote a letter, entrusting it to Liang to bring to Shanghai. Liang has now met with lawyer Yao Zhaoli to discuss everything.

Stating Aspirations

When Liang met with lawyer Yao Zhaoli, he recounted his experiences in resisting Japan and stated that due to various circumstances, his life was very difficult. He intended to rent a rickshaw and pull it on the streets to carry passengers, so that he could eke out a living and wait for the opportunity to resist Japan again in the future. Lawyer Yao repeatedly persuaded him and offered to provide financial assistance, but Liang firmly refused, saying that young people like him should support themselves through labor and should not rely on others.

Rickshaw Pulling Life

Liang has been pulling a rickshaw since yesterday. Lawyer Yao has completed the rental procedures on his behalf. The rickshaw Liang pulls has a concession license number of 4678 and a Chinese area license number of 14678. It belongs to Wang Feihong's rickshaw company. The rent is 65 cents (currency unspecified) per day. However, Liang's residence cannot be announced due to other considerations.

Pudong Residents Strive to Preserve the Old Xidu Wharf; the 27th Branch of the 5th District Petitions the Higher Party Headquarters for Review

Regarding the case of the British company Asiatic Petroleum Company encroaching and merging the old Xidu Wharf in Pudong, the nearby residents, seeing that the gateway to Pudong would be blocked, are extremely indignant. Recently, the company has even hired workers to begin construction. The residents, in a moment of desperation, gathered over a hundred women to the site to stop the construction. The situation at the time was quite serious. For three consecutive days, the two sides persisted. Fortunately, the public security police were able to maintain order and prevent any incidents. Now, the company, seeing that its wishes have not been fulfilled, ordered all workers yesterday to cease blocking construction. Male and female workers working in various cotton mills in North Pudong also took the opportunity to force ferries to carry passengers to and from the wharf, restoring it to its former state. According to insiders, the company is now planning to devise a proper solution, first opening a small road to Pudong at the eastern end of the wharf and building a bridge over the road in its original form, in order to appease the public. However, the public believes that this claim has not been verified and fears that the company will revert to its old ways, so they firmly adhere to their unyielding spirit and fight to the end. Yesterday, they also sent representatives to petition Mr. Pan Zhiwen, a local gentry in Yangjing Town, requesting him to ask Mr. Du Yue, a standing committee member of the Pudong Tongsheng Township Association, for his assistance in achieving the goal of preserving the original state of the old Xidu Wharf. Mr. Pan expressed his acceptance and promised to convey their request. The party branches in the 20th and 27th districts of the 5th district have also separately submitted petitions to the 5th district party headquarters for review after receiving the residents' requests for assistance in preserving the old road. The original petition from the 27th branch is excerpted below:

Petition regarding the Asiatic Petroleum Company Lower Depot Wharf obtaining approval to block the road and merge the newly purchased base, requesting consideration for the Pudong gateway and facilitation of public transportation in order to promote municipal prosperity. It has been found that the Asiatic Petroleum Company Lower Depot Wharf has purchased the vacant land of the Hefeng Shipyard and, under the guise of municipal government approval, has blocked and encroached the original Xidu Wharf, merging it with the new land. This is a legitimate request for a merchant, but it is inappropriate to consider the widening of Xipu Road as a satisfactory condition. Xipu Road originally had an eight-foot road, which has now been widened. Although more than one hundred feet of the Pudong waterfront have been conceded, the former Tanggong Shanhou Bureau submitted a memorandum to the Shanghai County Magistrate on July 15th of the Republic of China, which was forwarded to the Jiangsu Negotiator and the Shanghai Circuit Intendant for review and then transferred to the Junpu Bureau for compliance. Except for Dongjiadu, the remaining areas should be surveyed according to the map, and all places where mud filling and elevation are reported should delineate ten zhang of the Pudong waterfront for public ferries. The established cases are all there, and there is nothing to hide. Furthermore, Xipu Road is five or six li away from the ferry crossing opposite the Meifu Oil Depot. If the Xidu Wharf is blocked, the factory workers in the middle of these two ends will inevitably move to the concession, which will increase the population of the concession. Other various obstacles to the future prosperity of the market, the construction of factories, and the loading and unloading of goods are too numerous to mention. An examination of the concession reveals that a public wharf for entering Pudong has been built every one thousand feet. Now, considering the Yangshupu section, from the Weituoma Road wharf eastward, there are four Pudong wharves at Andong Road, Qiwupu Road, and Lan Road. The intention is to facilitate transportation and promote the market. Can we not pay attention to Pudong? If the authorities are concerned about treaty relations and find it difficult to cancel the approval, then, in any case, a Pudong road and wharf should be left between Asiatic Petroleum Company and Hefeng Shipyard before construction is allowed. Otherwise, the villagers will only care about sovereignty and not know the harm, and accidents are likely to occur, which is very worrying. In order to prevent accidents, the branch cannot remain silent. It has been submitted to the fifth party member congress for discussion, and it has been resolved to submit it to your association for review. Please approve the forwarding, which will be convenient for the party. Respectfully submitted.

Hospital or Roulette? A Major Fraud Case of Ten Thousand Yuan Between Chinese and Austrians; One Austrian Detained, One Fled; the French Concession Police Also Accuse the Plaintiff and Defendant of Bribery and Forgery

According to the Huadong News Agency, yesterday afternoon, the Second Special District Court of this port rendered a verdict in a major fraud case between Chinese and foreigners. The plaintiff was Chinese Wang Meiting, and the defendants were Austrians Sebersok and Bi Cha. German pharmacist Miller, reporter Sheng Like, and Ms. Tang Jin were also involved as witnesses. The content of the case was extremely complicated. The plaintiff's complaint stated that the two defendants took 100,000 yuan (currency unspecified) on the pretext of jointly opening a hospital, while the defendants claimed that it was not for opening a hospital, but for jointly establishing a roulette gambling house. Because of this, the French Concession Police also filed a complaint, accusing the plaintiff and defendant of public bribery, and accusing the plaintiff of forgery. The French Concession Police's case is to be heard in two weeks. As for the case of Wang Meiting suing Austrians Sebersok and Bi Cha, it was judged yesterday that the first defendant, Sebersok, must return 100,000 yuan (currency unspecified) to the plaintiff and pay a fine of 1,000 yuan (currency unspecified). Because he was unable to pay, he was immediately detained. The court ruled that the fine could be commuted at the rate of three yuan per day of imprisonment. The second defendant, Bi Cha, is on the run, and the police authorities have been ordered to apprehend him. The incident occurred in June of this year. At that time, the plaintiff, Wang Meiting, met the first defendant, Austrian Sebersok, and the second defendant, Austrian Bi Cha, in social circles, and their friendship deepened. Wang wanted to set up a hospital, and Sebersok and Bi Cha also had this idea, so they entered into an agreement to cooperate, with Wang contributing 100,000 yuan (currency unspecified), which was given to Sebersok and Bi Cha to be responsible for the operation. At that time, German doctor Miller, reporter Sheng Like, and Ms. Tang Jin were invited to be witnesses. However, after the two defendants took Wang's 100,000 yuan (currency unspecified), they used evasive language and did not establish a hospital. Wang suspected that something was wrong and began an investigation, and Bi Cha suddenly secretly returned to his country at this time. Sebersok also fabricated a false name and asked the Austrian consulate for a passport to return to his country. Wang was greatly alarmed and immediately filed a lawsuit in court, arresting the first defendant, Sebersok. After several interrogations, Sebersok admitted that Wang had contributed 100,000 yuan (currency unspecified), of which more than 80,000 yuan (currency unspecified) was taken, but it was for jointly setting up a roulette gambling house, not for setting up a hospital. Witness Miller also said that Wang was opening a gambling house and invited him to work there, with a monthly salary of 500 yuan (currency unspecified). He himself did not know what gambling was. In addition, Sheng Like and Ms. Tang Jin testified that the agreement at the time was for the establishment of a hospital. Sheng Like also said that because the languages of the two parties were not clear, he acted as a translator, and what they discussed was purely for the establishment of a hospital. Therefore, the testimonies in this case were conflicting. Until yesterday morning, Judge Wu ascended the bench to render a verdict, fining the first defendant 1,000 yuan (currency unspecified). Since he could not pay, the fine was commuted at the rate of three yuan per day of imprisonment. The second defendant is still being pursued. The police's case is scheduled to be heard in two weeks.

Pujiang No. 5 Ferry Boat Trial Voyage Yesterday; the Shanghai Ferry Route Extended to Wusong; the Most Exquisite Ferry in East Asia

Since the city took over the ferry business in this city, it has been very developed due to proper management. Now, the No. 5 ferry boat sailing between Wusong and Tongren Wharf has been completed. Yesterday afternoon, it hosted all sectors of society on the ferry boat, and sailed to Sanjiakou, Wusong at 2:30 pm, and then returned to Shanghai. The details are recorded as follows:

Grandeur of the Trial Voyage

Yesterday was the first trial voyage of the ferry boat. The company invited Chinese and Western people from this port to participate, accompanied by the Public Security Bureau military band. Those present included Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, Director of the Finance Bureau Cai Zengji, Director of the Public Works Bureau Xu Peihuang, Director of the Navigation Bureau Zhu Yaoting, Director of the International Telephone Bureau City Ferry No. 5

Wen Yuqing, Executive Director of Xingye Trust Company Wu Yunzhai, Director of the City Treasury Wu Zixiang, City Government Secretaries Tang Shixuan, Chen Kecheng, Geng Jiaji, Wang Shaozhai, Chief of the General Affairs Office of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau Xu Yuanfang, Municipal Council Member He De Kui Tan Shaoliang, Secretary of the Two Roads Management Bureau Qin Hancai, and more than two hundred reporters from Chinese and Western newspapers. The ferry boat first docked at the Tongren Wharf on the Bund, Nanjing Road at 10:00 AM. After the guests signed in, each was given a photo of the new ferry boat by the ushers as a souvenir. At 2:30 PM, the music started and the boat departed, followed by the cross-river ferry boats operated by the company at both ends. It passed the various docks without stopping, reaching Wusong in only 3:40. On the way back, the company specially prepared exquisite refreshments to entertain the guests. It returned to the Tongren Wharf at 5:00. The sky was high and the air was crisp that day, and the guests enjoyed the autumn scenery of the Pujiang River and returned with pleasure.

Mayor's Visit

Mayor Wu and others arrived at the Tongren Wharf at 1:00 PM and were accompanied by Tan Boying, Director of the Municipal Ferry Administration, to board the ferry boat for a visit, especially the first and second class cabins and the engine room. Mayor Wu praised the exquisite equipment and clean layout of the ferry boat. He then had some refreshments in the first-class cabin before leaving. It is said that the ferry boat is the only exquisite ferry boat in East Asia.

Origins of Construction

The Shanghai Xingye Trust Company, which manages the Pujiang River ferries in this city, has spared no effort in expanding and improving them. There are now no fewer than a dozen new ferry boats, large and small, which are convenient for travelers on both sides of the Pujiang River. Currently, the only long ferry line runs from the Tongren Wharf in Shanghai through Xidu Qing Temple, etc., to Donggou and Gaoqiao. The traffic in the Youchi area, Laoshusha, and Wusong, which are designated by the municipal government, is still inconvenient. Therefore, the company spent a large sum of 150,000 yuan (currency unspecified) to add a No. 5 large ferry boat to the existing four long ferry boats, extending the route to Wusong and completing the transportation construction of the northern section of the Pujiang River.

Construction Overview

The ferry boat is 120 feet long, 21 feet wide, 9.5 feet deep, and has a draft of 5.5 feet. It has a displacement of 195 tons and is powered by a six-cylinder, 334-horsepower diesel engine, with a speed of 12 nautical miles. It can carry 600 passengers. The lower level is the second-class cabin, all with reclining chairs, painted with first-class Beijing lacquer. Each seat has triangular wooden strips to prevent passengers from lying down. The light and air are very sufficient, which is unmatched by any other river boat. The front part of the middle level is the first-class cabin with seats, all made of teak. The chair backs are made according to the curve of the human back. The rear part is the second-class loose cabin, which also carries goods. The upper level is the special-class cabin, located in the middle, with a wine counter made of Italian marble. There is a heating stove in winter, which uses the heat from the diesel engine to increase the temperature in the cabin. The exquisite interior decoration is no less than that of foreign ocean-going ships. Even the smallest clothes hook has its own special advantages. The door and window switches and door locks are all custom-made by a famous German factory that imitates those used in the Berlin subway. The deck is made of teak and polished by machine. In terms of safety, there are sufficient lifebuoys and life rafts. The fire-fighting equipment, in addition to fire extinguishing chemicals, is also equipped with fire hydrants on each floor, which can be said to be double safety. In terms of technology, the whole boat is full of water lines. The lower part is equipped with two eight-inch wide water floating roads. Even when fully loaded with passengers, there is no risk of tilting. The bow of the ship adopts the latest warship style. If it does not collide with other ships, there is no risk of the lower part of the waterline being hit. The ship's hull is streamline, shaped like a fish's back. This is the first time it has been used in the Eastern shipbuilding industry. Its advantages are that it is easy to turn and it increases the speed of travel. Overall, the equipment of the ship is such that the first-class and second-class cabins are clean and simple, suitable for ordinary passengers. The special-class cabin is refined, elegant, and beautiful, suitable for tourists. In fact, it can meet the needs of various types of passengers. This is the special advantage of the ferry boat.

The Male Child's Corpse in Longhua Was an Elementary School Student; His Mother Claimed the Corpse and Coffin Yesterday; the Reason for the Murder Is Unknown

A report was made in this paper regarding the discovery of the murdered boy, with lacerations to his head, chest, abdomen and feet, on the vacant land of the Xuanjia Residence of Longhua Cement Factory on the night of the 25th of this month, which prompted the District Court to examine and collect evidence. It is learned that Ding Yin, wife of the late Ding A'san of Wuxi, age 49, went to the Ninth District Bao Wu Jixsheng's office yesterday morning, who accompanied her to the District Court to claim the body. Her family operates the Ding Juxing San Ji Iron Shop on Xiaoshadu Road, Kangding Road, and their business is quite prosperous. Her family also owns more than 20 mu of land. After her husband's death, she was left with an only son named Ding Fugen, age 13. Because he was studying recently, he was enrolled at the Baxianqiao Law School. Because it was inconvenient to travel back and forth, he lived at the Zhang Yuxing Iron Shop opened by his uncle Zhang Genfa at No. 123 Laohai Road. After school every day, he never went out. On the afternoon of the 25th of this month, he did not return home after school. The family searched everywhere without success, so they posted a reward of 100 yuan (currency unspecified) to find him. Her son was wearing a half-new dark blue long gown, a dark green velvet vest, a faux wool gabardine trousers, and basketball shoes. And seeing the report that the day the boy was murdered in Longhua was the same day her son went missing, and the clothes and age matched, she requested permission to claim the corpse and coffin, and to apprehend and prosecute the murderer. She also claimed that there were no threatening letters before her son went missing, and no ransom letters afterwards, so it was not a kidnapping. And the child had no enemies, and she did not know why anyone would want to cut off her family's lineage, which caused her unbearable pain. She was given a preliminary hearing by Prosecutor Yang An, who immediately ordered the Bao to accompany her to identify and claim the corpse and coffin, pending investigation and thorough examination.

Arrest of the Murderer of Tang Jiapeng, Former Manager of the Great World; The Mastermind and Main Culprit Are Still at Large

Tang Jiapeng, a native of Ningbo and 44 years old, was the former manager of the Great World amusement park, residing at No. 3, Wufuli, Luzon Road, in the French Concession. On June 18th of this year, around 1:00 AM, Tang was preparing to return home from the Great World. As soon as he exited the amusement park's main gate and stepped onto his Austin car (French Concession License No. 7065), his chauffeur, Xu Arong, was about to start the engine when a group of thugs suddenly jumped out from the crowd by the roadside and opened fire indiscriminately. Tang was hit by five bullets all over his body. By the time the car reached Baolong Hospital, he had already succumbed to his injuries and died en route. A stray bullet also killed Wu Guangcai, a Yangzhou bath attendant (33 years old) who scrubbed backs at the Jiquan Bathhouse in Beichujiaqiao. The details were reported in this newspaper. Since the incident, the French police have attached great importance to it, repeatedly instructing all detectives to solve the case within a time limit. However, after the incident, the perpetrators, realizing that the search was too intense and knowing it would be difficult to remain in this city, fled to other areas to avoid detection. The detectives handling the case, although aware that these people had fled far away, feared that tracking and arresting them would be counterproductive. Therefore, they remained calm and eased the situation, knowing that their escape was only temporary and that they would eventually return to Shanghai. As expected, yesterday afternoon around 1:00 PM, Inspector-General Jin Jiulin suddenly received a confidential report from his subordinates stating that Zhang Xiaosizi, a suspect in the case, had secretly returned to Shanghai and was hiding somewhere on Haifang Road in the International Settlement. He requested immediate arrest. Inspector-General Jin immediately led Detective Zhang Ziying, Qian Yumin, Deputy Detective Zhou Yaoting, Detectives Xu Guilin, Cui Zhenguo, and Chinese and foreign detectives from the Gordon Road Police Station, and drove to No. 648, Haifang Road, to the Tiger Stove shop. Zhang was inside drinking tea and was arrested. Taken to the police station for interrogation, Zhang confessed that he was 26 years old, from Funing, and had previously served as a member of the Jiangbei Security Corps. He admitted that the killing of Tang was commissioned by someone else. On the day of the attack, they had rented Room No. 8 at the Asia Hotel at 135 Avenue Edward VII, where more than ten people planned the murder. The first plan was to disguise themselves as small vendors selling pancakes, fruit, and other items and kill Tang at his house in Wufuli, Luzon Road. However, due to the long-term presence of gatekeepers and police at the entrance of the alley, it was difficult to carry out. Therefore, they decided to change their plan and attack him at the entrance of the Great World, where there would be a dense crowd of people in the evening, with many tourists, making it easier to escape. That night, he and his accomplices Wang Jinkui and Zhou Ermujiang, each carrying a pistol, went to the Great World. When Tang came out, Wang Jinkui fired three shots at him first. Seeing that Tang was still not dead and trying to escape, Zhou Ermujiang fired six more shots. After achieving their goal, they fled back to the Asia Hotel and hid on Haifang Road until his arrest. According to the police, since the mastermind is still at large, the authorities have ordered all detectives to rigorously pursue the main culprit and bring him to justice for interrogation.

Editorial Outline of "A Grand View of Shanghai," Compiled by Zhou Shixun at the Request of the Wenhua Company

Mr. Zhou Shixun, editor of the Wenhua Fine Arts Publishing and Printing Company's film monthly, has recently compiled a book titled "A Grand View of Shanghai." The book, with over 200 pages, is entirely photographic and showcases all aspects of Shanghai as designed and categorized by Mr. Zhou for the Chinese audience. Each photograph includes detailed explanations, or historical accounts of famous landmarks. To facilitate foreign tourists visiting China, the explanations are translated into simple English. The book contains approximately 1,000 photographs, printed with three-color, two-color, and single-color halftone plates on high-quality paper. The editorial outline and table of contents are divided into four categories: Clothing, Food, Housing, and Transportation, with over 100 subcategories. Each category features approximately ten photographs, such as the grandeur of Greater Shanghai, the municipal administration of the Chinese territory, the municipal administration and police of the International Settlement, major institutions in Shanghai, universities, girls' schools, transportation, historical sites, etc. These are all sufficient to make readers feel the greatness of the sea. Additionally, topics such as Shanghai's strange events and places, Shanghai's contradictory psychology, and the path to Shanghai's downfall can all provide readers with profound warnings. Other topics such as the introduction of hotels, restaurants, and amusement parks, as well as seasonal entertainment in spring, summer, autumn, and winter, provide detailed guidance, while simultaneously implying how to avoid being taken advantage of. In short, while there are many guidebooks for Shanghai, there has never been a guide to Shanghai that emphasizes both text and images. "A Grand View of Shanghai" is the first of its kind. The book has now been fully compiled and will be printed soon. Readers from all over have been eagerly pre-ordering it from the company, and wholesale orders from Southeast Asia are particularly active, indicating the need for this type of book among readers in distant places. According to Mr. Zhou, the book's editor, the entire compilation process has long been completed, but the collection of a large amount of material had to be postponed by half a month. This time, he can guarantee on-time publication. The address of Wenhua Publishing is at the intersection of Henan Road and Sijing Road. The book is priced at three yuan per copy, with an 80% discount for pre-orders.

Incoming Mail

Two Major Principles of Controlled Economy

— Mu Ouchu

Humans are born with a group and therefore born with a social life. When humans began to engage in social life, "division of labor" also occurred.

Division of labor is the most important means to increase production capacity and is a means to unleash infinite and great production capacity. This is undoubtedly a fact. Henry Ford, the American automobile king, once said, "Further division of labor is the key to increasing production." Economist Adam Smith also regarded division of labor as the first element in increasing national wealth in his famous book "The Wealth of Nations." He cited the division of labor in the needle-making industry as an example, saying that division of labor can increase a person's productivity by 4,800 times, and recently, some people have said that division of labor can increase human power by tens of thousands, or even millions of times.

Under the ancient large family system, the division of labor based on gender has been confirmed by economic historians. However, this division of labor occurs due to the natural necessity of human life, so the increase in its productivity is limited and cannot be unlimited. As for the more concrete initial division of labor, it is based on occupation, that is, the work that used to be done by one person is first divided into carpenters, blacksmiths, merchants, etc., becoming a specialized occupation. The more developed the economy, the tighter this occupational division of labor becomes.

This division of labor method can be roughly divided into two categories: one is the same occupation, but because the items they manufacture are different, they each specialize in what they manufacture. For example, carpenters are divided into carpenters who build houses, carpenters who build ships, and carpenters who do fine work. The other is to divide a production process that used to be done by one person into several manufacturing processes, each engaging in a part of the work, such as spinning, weaving, and dyeing. Further division of labor then leads to each person only doing a part of the work. Dozens or hundreds of people each perform different tasks, which can then complete an overall operation.

To make it easier to understand, the progress of division of labor and its differentiation methods are shown in the diagram below:

Occupational Division of Labor

Life 丨 Undifferentiated Labor 　　　　　　　　 Specialized Technical Division of Labor

Occupational 　　Occupational 　　Technical Division of Labor

Division of Labor

Productive 　　Technical Division of Labor

Division of Labor 　　Technical Division of Labor

Now, let me illustrate this with an example. Taking housing as an example, if we want to build a house, we must first have ordinary construction workers, and then we must gather carpenters, plasterers, and other kinds of workers. Among the carpenters, in addition to ordinary carpenters, there are also specialized fine carpenters. If we consider the aspect of goods, the wood processed by the carpenters must have loggers and transporters as its source, as well as trains, ships, and lumber companies that saw the wood into planks, and transportation companies that transport the planks, as well as various other merchants. In the train, ship, and lumber companies, there are various specialized workers, and these train, ship, and lumber companies are all formed by integrating the labor of thousands of people in various specialized fields. Housing is like this, and other things such as clothing and food are no different. Only in this way can each production be carried out in accordance with economic principles. Through the accumulation of these products, our cultural life is becoming more and more advanced. Therefore, division of labor is the foundation of human cultural life.

Although division of labor is the foundation of human cultural life, there is another important condition that we should not neglect. This condition is the adjustment of each part. In other words, after division of labor, how can we ensure that there are no contradictions or conflicts between the separate tasks, and how can we give them the most reasonable and purposeful connection? This question is the most important. Today's scientific management methods, industrial rationalization, and even the so-called controlled economy are all aimed at solving this problem and promoting methods. Let us now further elaborate on the issue of adjusting each part. (To be continued)

Education News

Ministry of Education Explains Regulations for Normal Schools and Secondary Schools

The Ministry of Education previously received a request from the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education for clarification regarding ambiguities in the regulations for Hangzhou Normal School and Provincial High Schools. Instructions for clarification were issued, but the original text was not published. Now, similar situations and questions have arisen in various provinces. The Ministry of Education's previous clarifications to the Zhejiang Department of Education are extracted below: (1) Boarding students at the secondary school are permitted to be exempt from evening self-study, but the school should devise methods for supervision and examination, and submit them to the Department of Education for review. (2) Starting from 1933, all graduating students must adhere to the secondary school regulations and participate in graduation examinations. (3) Students enrolled before 1933 must also comply with Articles 50 to 65 of the secondary school regulations. (4) Article 62 of the secondary school regulations, which states that "all should be demoted to the lower semester's class for study," simply means what is commonly referred to as repeating a grade. (5) Article 63 of the secondary school regulations, which states that "continue to audit courses with the original class," refers to students who have passed all subjects in that grade and are auditing courses in the same grade. (6) Article 63 of the secondary school regulations, which states "simultaneously seek ways to remediate the relevant subjects," the subjects for remediation are not limited to outside of class time within the teaching schedule, but also allows for free remediation. The supplementary exams for failed subjects can be moved to a few days before the next semester for flexible arrangements. The same article refers to students who fail one subject's supplementary exam. Repeating a grade non-consecutively is not subject to the "limited to one time" rule. (7) For students starting in the spring semester, Article 69 of the secondary school regulations already stipulates that the average of the student's grades for the upper and lower semesters should still be used as the student's academic year grade, and the academic year grade must be reported when submitting the student's academic performance report. (8) Article 64 of the secondary school regulations has a provision for those who fail the graduation examination, "should be required to repeat a grade for one academic year." However, given that the school has complete grades starting in both the spring and autumn semesters, it can be specially permitted to change this to repeating a grade for one semester. As for the remedial coursework methods after repeating a grade, the school can consider the situation and provide opportunities for remedial classes for failed subjects, without requiring every subject to be taken in the third academic year.

General Regulations of the Boy Scouts of China (Continued from yesterday) Chapter 5: Boy Scout Servicemen of China

Article 11: Any citizen of the Republic of China who is at least twenty-one years old, possesses knowledge and experience in Boy Scouting, and is willing to serve the Boy Scout cause, may apply to become a Boy Scout Serviceman of China in accordance with the law.

Article 12: Boy Scout Servicemen of China shall be examined and classified into several grades according to their knowledge and experience.

Article 13: Separate regulations shall be established regarding the various regulations for Boy Scout Servicemen of China.

Chapter 6: Organization of the Management Agencies of the Boy Scouts of China

Section 1: General Association of the Boy Scouts of China

Subsection 1: Members

Article 14: The following categories of personnel may become members of the General Association of the Boy Scouts of China after undergoing formal procedures. Their qualifications, responsibilities, and membership procedures shall be determined separately: (1) Those who directly participate in the Boy Scout cause, (2) Those who support the Boy Scout cause in spirit and material, (3) Those who are enthusiastic about social undertakings and are models for children.

Subsection 2: President and Vice-Presidents

Article 15: The General Association of the Boy Scouts of China shall have one President and two Vice-Presidents, who shall be selected and appointed by the Central Executive Committee of the Kuomintang. The selection of the President shall be limited to those who have held the highest national office. The President and Vice-Presidents shall all be honorary positions and shall not be responsible for the administrative affairs of the Association.

Article 16: The President shall be the highest honorary leader of the Boy Scouts of China. His tasks are as follows: (1) To lead the Boy Scouts of China, (2) To lead the members of the Association in developing various undertakings, (3) To represent the General Association and the Boy Scouts of China externally, (4) To review Boy Scouts nationwide, (5) To award various honorary medals.

Article 17: The Vice-Presidents shall assist the President in developing the Association's undertakings. (To be continued)

Shanghai Children's Welfare Association Plans to Establish Nurseries; Three Types: General, Labor, and Vagrant; Type A Regulations Passed at Second Standing Committee Meeting Yesterday; Banquet Hosted for Leaders from All Walks of Life; Xu Shiying and Others Attended

The Shanghai Children's Welfare Association hosted a banquet for leaders from all walks of life at the Hong Kong Road Bank Club at 12:00 noon yesterday and held its second standing committee meeting to discuss important cases such as the establishment of nurseries. Details are recorded as follows:

Banquet for All Sectors

Those who attended included Mayor Wu (represented by Pan Gongzhan), Director Pan, Li Tingan (representing Wu Liguo), Xu Shiying, Wang Xiaolai, Zhu Ziqiao, Wang Yiting, Lin Kanghou, Xi Guansheng, Feng Yitang, Hu Xiyuan, Qin Runqing, Zhao Jinqing, Zhu Yinjiang, Yin Guansan, Qiu Qisheng, Chen Lengseng, Hu Shuyi, Gong Yushuo, Shen Ziheng, Chen Bai, Chen Jicheng, Wu Yunchu, Chen Hongqin, Mei Yunying, Liu Wang Liming, Gao Jinglang, Yang Maorong, Zhao Zengqi, Li Zushen, Wang Guanyi, Zhou Wanghe, etc. During the banquet, Pan Gongzhan first reported, stating that the association plans to establish nurseries to supplement family education, reduce the burden on families, and care for impoverished children. The nurseries will be divided into three types: general, labor, and vagrant. It is planned to complete three nurseries in the shortest possible time, with an estimated startup cost of approximately 3,000 yuan per nursery. He requested that people from all walks of life who are enthusiastic about social welfare strongly support this cause. Subsequently, Li Zushen, Wang Xiaolai, Mei Yunying, Liu Wang Liming, and others expressed their opinions. Prominent figures from all walks of life expressed great approval, and enthusiastic donations of several thousand yuan were made on the spot. The banquet concluded with a group photo at 2:00 PM.

Second Standing Committee Meeting

The second standing committee meeting was held at 2:00 PM. Those in attendance were Pan Gongzhan, Li Tingan (representing Wu Liguo), Chen Heqin, Zhao Zengqi, Hu Shuyi, Wang Guanyi, Liu Wang Liming, with Zhou Wanghe present as an observer. Pan Gongzhan presided, and Zhou Wanghe served as the secretary. Formalities were observed, and the chairman first reported that the Booksellers Association had confirmed Zhang Shuliang as their representative to the association as a committee member. The following matters were then discussed: (1) The proposal for the Type A nursery management regulations was passed, with amendments resolved. (2) The proposal to hire Wang Xiaolai and others as fundraising committee members was resolved to request the standing committee members to nominate them and submit them to the next standing committee meeting for approval. (3) The proposal for the Shanghai Children's Welfare Association fundraising method was passed, with amendments resolved. (4) The proposal for the preparatory committee for the Zhabei Childhood Experimental Zone, jointly organized by the association and the China Childhood Welfare Association, was resolved to request that those already hired by the China Childhood Welfare Association be additionally hired. (5) The proposal for the date and location of the standing committee meetings was resolved to be held on the second Friday of each month at 4:00 PM at the Lianhuan Society. (6) The proposal to draft a method for Children's Day was resolved to assign Committee Member Hu Shuyi to draft it and submit it to the next standing committee meeting for approval and submission to the municipal government for promulgation. (7) The proposal to draft Type B and Type C nursery regulations was resolved to request Committee Members Wang and Hu to be responsible for drafting them and submitting them to the nursery group for approval. The meeting was adjourned after the discussions.

Type A Regulations

The association's nurseries are divided into three types: Type A general nurseries, Type B labor nurseries, and Type C vagrant nurseries. The Type A management regulations have been passed as follows: (1) Purpose: The purpose of this nursery is to supplement family education, reduce the burden on families, and care for children from impoverished families. The results of the experiment will be announced to the public to facilitate promotion. (2) Scope: This nursery is exclusively for children from ordinary families. Parents who are unable to educate and care for their children due to occupational or environmental reasons may send their children to this nursery for care in accordance with the regulations (procedures to be determined separately). (3) Establishment: This nursery is established by the Shanghai Children's Welfare Association as a nursery undertaking. (4) Departments: In order to meet the needs of ordinary society and to facilitate education and management, the nursery is divided into an infant department (newborn to one year old), a toddler department (one to three years old), and a kindergarten department (three to six years old), regardless of gender. (5) Time: The nursery offers both daytime care and day-and-night care. Children in daytime care are sent to the nursery by their families in the morning and picked up in the afternoon. The nursery provides lunch and afternoon tea (time to be determined separately). Children in day-and-night care have their meals and lodging provided by the nursery, except for clothing and other items, which are provided by their families. Their families may visit or pick them up once on Sundays. (6) Quota: To be determined separately according to social needs. (7) Term: The term of care for children is one year for infants, two years for toddlers, and three years for kindergarten students, with a maximum of six years. (8) Education and Care: (A) The nursery emphasizes scientific care, lively guidance, and a stimulating environment for children, with suitable equipment. The curriculum will be determined separately. (B) A parent-teacher meeting is held once a month, which all family members of the children must attend in order to connect and communicate. (C) Visits: Children may be visited once a week. If there are any corrections to be made regarding the children's education, hygiene, and habits, the family should make every effort to cooperate in order to achieve perfection. (9) Fees: All those in care must pay a fee, which is prepaid monthly. However, the nursery may increase or decrease the fee for children with special circumstances. The amount of the fee will be specified in a separate table. (10) Supplementary Provisions: These regulations shall be implemented after approval by the Shanghai Children's Welfare Association.

List of Committee Members

In addition to Pan Gongzhan as a committee member by default, the Zhare Undertaking Group has hired Hu Shuyi, Chen Bai, Chen Lengseng, Chen Qingchun, Qiu Xisheng, Liu Wang Liming, Wang Guanyi, Chen Jicheng, Feng Yitang, Shen Tong, Yin Guanzhi, Yang Maorong, Gong Yushuo, Wu Liguo, Mei Yunying, Gao Jinglang, Jiang Shideng, and others as committee members.

Fundraising Methods

(1) In order to raise funds for various children's undertakings in the city, the Fundraising Committee of the Association is organized in accordance with Article 4 of the Association's Simple Rules. (2) The members of this committee shall be nominated by the Standing Committee of the Association and appointed by the President of the Association. (3) The President of the Association and the Chairman of the Standing Committee are ex officio members. (4) The powers of this committee are as follows: (A) Responsible for raising the Association's fund, (B) Responsible for raising the Association's various temporary expenses, (C) Responsible for allocating and reviewing the use and accounts of the Association's various fundraising expenses, (D) Planning the basic fundraising methods for the Association's fund and temporary expenses. (5) All members of this committee are honorary officials. (6) Any matters not covered in these Simple Rules may be amended at any time and submitted to the President for approval and amendment. (7) These Simple Rules shall be implemented after being passed by the Standing Committee of the Association and submitted to the President for approval.

The Uneven Distribution of Talent Leads Youyou to Lose to Banque de l'Indochine: A Score of Four to Eight; The Assembled Stars of Banque de l'Indochine Prove to be Formidable Opponents

Since Jiang Shanqing, Chen Jiaqiu, Zhong Yongsen, and Liang Shutang, along with four warriors from Jinan, joined Youyou, the Youyou lineup has been refreshed and its strength enhanced. However, unfortunately, in their first match of the West League yesterday, they encountered the formidable Banque de l'Indochine and suffered a setback, losing by a score of four to eight. The referee was Botto.

Banque de l'Indochine Lineup

Garnier, J. Walter

Boggis, B. Huot

Fulu Shou, Pike, Collet

Nicolas Leff, W. Walter

Remédi, Favrel

Youyou Lineup

Liang Shutang, Li Shuoyou

Wang Shusen, Sun Jinshun

Wang Caigao, Huang Ruihua, Hu Youcheng

Jiang Shanqing, Chen Jiaqiu

The Youyou Lineup Still Needs Improvement

Jiang Shanqing as the inner defender, Liang Shutang as the forward, Chen Jiaqiu as the inner striker, and Zhong Yongsen as the right winger are all outstanding players. Coupled with Youyou's original strength, they should be able to compete with Banque de l'Indochine. However, they ended up losing by a score of eight to four, indicating that their lineup and defense urgently need improvement. The collapse of the center-back line yesterday was the team's fatal weakness. Huang Ruihua is old, Shi Jinsheng lacks the strength, and Liang Shutang is isolated and helpless. With the center line failing, the inner defenders were extremely busy, and Wang Caigao bore the brunt, greatly disappointing everyone. At the same time, the central leader of the five forwards failed to achieve the effect of connected arms, resulting in twice the effort with half the result. Youyou has been making progress in recent years and should not ignore this point in order to live up to the audience's expectations.

The Strength of Banque de l'Indochine is Surprisingly Remarkable

Banque de l'Indochine has a concentration of talent and a well-organized lineup. They have previously played against the Shanghai Municipal Team and the Hong Kong Team, and observers do not underestimate them despite their losses, considering them to be a strong team in this year's West League. The team is based on the original personnel of Banque de l'Indochine, absorbing famous players from the West, Portugal, and Lux teams, creating a hybrid that can dominate everything. Their victory over Youyou was within their expectations. Judging from their performance yesterday, their rushing, passing, and shooting were all excellent, with only the left inner defender having some shortcomings. When they take the stage again in the future, they will be truly impeccable.

Gains and Losses Within Five Minutes

Youyou kicked off at the beginning of the day, but their progress was unfavorable, and martial law was declared in front of the goal. A ball suddenly broke out of the encirclement, and Zhong Yongsen charged into the array alone. Boggis fell for the trick, and Zhong made a well-placed pass. Shuoyou met the ball in front of the goal and successfully scored. Overjoyed, the enemy soldiers invaded, and Favrel moved from the right to the center, and Collet lightly headed the ball in. The goalkeeper could not defend both sides, and the ball also went in. It was difficult to gain a point, but too easy to lose one. This is why Youyou's morale was low. Chen Jiaqiu and Zhong Yongsen exchanged passes and played well, but the opponent's goalkeeper, Fulu Shou, was indeed skilled and made several desperate saves, which was not easy to overcome. At that time, their momentum was still strong, and if the central players had eyes at their feet, they could have scored at least one or two goals.

Four Goals Lost Mysteriously

With Banque de l'Indochine's interior as solid as a fortress and their five forwards as lively as dragons and tigers, Youyou had no choice but to adopt a conservative strategy. Wang Caigao was surrounded and at a loss. Initially, he received help from Jiang and Liang, but he could not hold on. As soon as his spirit waned, the lineup became chaotic. B. Huot broke into the center alone (two to one). Remédi sent a long ball, and Wang Caigao panicked and shot the ball into his own goal. Banque de l'Indochine took a three-to-one lead. From then on, the gate was wide open, and the enemy continued to invade. Walter, the left winger, then scored a goal, and Favrel, the right winger, also made a great contribution. Sun Jinshun led his team in a counterattack and, with great effort, snatched a goal from the enemy, making the score five to two, with Banque de l'Indochine leading at halftime.

Efforts to Manuever Proved Unsuccessful

Although Youyou was behind, their morale was still strong, and Banque de l'Indochine was in a trapped position. Zhong and Li on the wings made contributions from time to time. Once, Zhong attacked himself, and the goalkeeper dived to catch the ball. Another time, he lobbed the ball in front of the goal, and Hu Youcheng competed with the goalkeeper. Li Shuoyou faced an empty goal but lobbed the ball over the post. Sun Jinshun dribbled the ball again and attacked, and Zhong passed the ball in again. Li Shuoyou finally lived up to expectations and made the score three to five. Just as they began to smile, tragedy struck again. Walter and Collet each scored another goal, making the score three to seven. Then, the general Jiang Shanqing suddenly left the field due to an ankle injury, and all hope of a comeback was extinguished. Liang Shutang bravely took on the important position of inner defender and fought hard against the strong enemy. Pike committed a foul at the fifteen-yard mark, and Sun and Zhong shot with their iron legs. The goalkeeper got the ball but lost it again, making the score four to seven. However, in the blink of an eye, Collet scored another goal, resulting in the final score of eight to four.

National Games to Return Site at End of Month; Preparations for Establishment of a Sports Academy and Memorial Park; Request to Borrow from the Memorial Park Management Committee

After the closing of the Fifth National Games, the various groups of the Organizing Committee moved back to the Ministry of Education on the 22nd and are currently rushing to complete the closing work, which can be completed in half a month. Regarding the transfer of the Central Stadium, according to reporters' inquiries to the Organizing Committee, when the National Games borrowed the site from the Memorial Park Management Committee of the Prime Minister, it was agreed to officially return it by the end of October. The venue and equipment have been largely cleaned up and are expected to be handed over on schedule. Regarding the future application of the sports field, since the next National Games has been decided to be held in Shanghai, there are still four years before the Seventh National Games. If the site is shelved, it would be too uneconomical. In order to save expenses, the Ministry of Education plans to establish a sports school in the Memorial Park, using the field to train sports professionals, so as to achieve two goals at once. However, this is still in the planning stage and needs to be discussed with the Memorial Park Management Committee for a final decision.
